Output (b): Dr. Sunil Shah of St George's at the University of London explains that bereavement can have a direct effect on the health of the heart, as their study found that the number of people who had a heart attack or stroke in the month after a loved one died was double that of a non-grieving control group. The British Heart Foundation states that "broken heart syndrome," or stress cardiomyopathy, is a temporary condition where the heart muscle becomes suddenly weakened or stunned, often brought on by a shock such as bereavement or other significant emotional or physical stress. An FAQ on broken heart syndrome published by Johns Hopkins University states that most heart attacks occur due to blockages and blood clots, while cardiomyopathy does not.
